<rating>5< /rating>< Text>
This is a great little capsule Target store taking residence on the corner and part of the first floor of an office building--right in the middle of the Financial District near Market Street. It's not a full size Target so, of course, don't expect them to carry everything a suburban Target store has. But they've got a small refrigerated section, fresh produce, and shelves with a small selection of food/snacks, a small selection of clothing, pharmacy/toiletries/beauty items/first aid/medications, etc. It's a Target with the basics needed for a city dweller or worker. It was super easy to swing by this location on a lunch break or after work, and grab the BART train on Market or make the walk down Market to the Ferry Building to catch a ferry out of the city.< /Text>

< Review>
Great place for many varieties of high quality dog food and cat food. Small selection for any other pet. Good options for grain free and healthy diets.

Most staff is well trained in their inventory.  Nice array of treats, toys, clothes, carriers, etc. For your four-legged family members.

They have cat trees in several styles as well as the usual line up of collars, harnesses and leashes.

Grooming station is on site in the store with good visiblity.

Prices are okay, better when you use the buy three get one free option.< /Review>

< Review>
There was a dog wash  station that was a hoot.  The shampoo was dispensed with the stream of water (like a car wash), then a switch turned off the shampoo so the dog could be rinsed, then the next switch turned on the blower.  The tubs were clean, and the drying station was raised for easy access to the dog.  The dryer was not so noisy so it might scare a dog,  yet the air stream was able to dry down to the skin.  My medium sized dog left fluffy, with soft fur from head to toe.  Nice attendants and people were there to help show me the ropes.<//Review>

< text>
Overall my experience here was ok. The price advertised can be a little misleading but with the eye exam (95.00) and 2 frames (95.00 for the most expensive pair, second one free) my total was 190.00 for 2 pairs of glasses. You do pay for what you get, the frames quality is ver sub-par compared to the Ray-Ban Wayfarers I had before so don't expect the best quality there, but the prescription was very comparable to the one I received at Lens Crafters and the optometrist did a great job. Even though the consultation was done via skype and she was not actually there physically. I did have a a price discrepency at the end which I had to call corporate about but the store manager came around and fixed it in the end. Overall if your looking for value this is probably your best bet.</text>

< review>
LOVE their food! And their $5 daily specials are just the right size to fill you up. This location was severely understaffed to the point that it looked like the employees were having to choose between filling orders quickly (which they weren't, even though the employees were clearly scrambling to fill them) and cleaning tables/maintaining the place. Because of this, they were out of lids at the drink area (which wasn't filled even after we told them within the 45 minutes or so we were there) and there was a huge package of napkins on the front counter that guests were expected to help themselves to. Despite all this, over all the appearance of the restaurant was good compared to many fast food places in the area.</review>
